      <p>
       This is a
       <b>
        list of solar eclipses in the 20th century
       </b>
       . During the period 1901 to 2000 there were 228
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_eclipses" title="Solar eclipses">
        solar eclipses
       </a>
       of which 78 were partial, 73 were annular (two
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse#Terminology" title="Solar eclipse">
        non-central
       </a>
       ), 71 were total (three non-central) and 6 were hybrids. The greatest number of eclipses in one year was five, in 1935, and one month, July 2000, had two eclipses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_catalog_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nasa_catalog-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_eclipses_of_the_20th_century">
        Notable eclipses of the 20th century
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_solar_eclipses_in_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Notable eclipses of the 20th century">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_May_29,_1919" title="Solar eclipse of May 29, 1919">
         29 May 1919
        </a>
        : this total eclipse was photographed by
        <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Eddington" title="Arthur Eddington">
         Arthur Eddington
        </a>
        to verify
        <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">
         general relativity
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-2">
          [2]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_June_20,_1955" title="Solar eclipse of June 20, 1955">
         20 June 1955
        </a>
        : longest total eclipse between 1901 and 2000, lasting a maximum of 7 minutes and 8 seconds
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-3">
          [3]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_June_30,_1973" title="Solar eclipse of June 30, 1973">
         30 June 1973
        </a>
        : a
        <a href="/wiki/Concorde" title="Concorde">
         Concorde
        </a>
        jet flew along the path, thereby extending the length of totality to 74 min.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-4">
          [4]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_March_29,_1987" title="Solar eclipse of March 29, 1987">
         29 March 1987
        </a>
        : second hybrid eclipse in less than one year, the first being on
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_October_3,_1986" title="Solar eclipse of October 3, 1986">
         1986 October 3
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_July_31,_2000" title="Solar eclipse of July 31, 2000">
         31 July 2000
        </a>
        : the second solar eclipse within one calendar month, the first being on
        <a href="/wiki/Solar_eclipse_of_July_1,_2000" title="Solar eclipse of July 1, 2000">
         2000 July 1
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Table">
        Table
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_solar_eclipses_in_the_20th_century&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Table">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The table gives the date and time of the greatest eclipse (in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dynamical_time" title="Dynamical time">
        dynamical time
       </a>
       , which in this case is the time when the axis of the Moon's shadow cone passes closest to the centre of Earth).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasa_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-nasa-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It also gives the type of eclipse (either Total, Annular, Partial or Hybrid) and for total and annular eclipses it gives the duration of the eclipse. The location of the greatest eclipse and the path width are also given, as well as the geographical areas affected.
      </p>

        </th>

            </th>
            <td class="navbox-list navbox-even" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
